\section{1. Data Loading and
Preprocessing}\label{data-loading-and-preprocessing}

\subsection{Study Area}\label{study-area}

The study area includes the major soybean-producing states of Illinois,
Indiana, and Iowa in the U.S. Corn Belt. County-level soybean yields
(bu/ac) and phenology-guided predictors are analyzed for the period
2018--2021.

\begin{figure}[H]

{\centering \includegraphics{index_files/mediabag/StudyArea.png}

}

\caption{Study area map showing Illinois, Indiana, and Iowa with average
soybean yields (bu/ac) from 2008 to 2021)}

\end{figure}%

\subsection{Dataset Overview}\label{dataset-overview}

\textbf{Data Download:} The data can also be directly downloaded from:
https://github.com/pouuh/phenology-guided-soybean-yield/releases/download/v1.0/soybean\_phenology\_guided\_dataset.zip

This section loads the pre-processed satellite-derived time series data
for soybean yield prediction. The dataset consists of:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Training Set}: Multi-temporal observations from multiple
  growing seasons
\item
  \textbf{Test Set}: Holdout data for final model evaluation
\item
  \textbf{Features}: 14 environmental variables captured at regular
  intervals throughout the growing season
\item
  \textbf{Target}: County-level soybean yield measurements (bushels per
  acre)
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Data Structure}\label{data-structure}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Input Shape}: \texttt{(samples,\ timesteps,\ features)} - 3D
  array representing time series
\item
  \textbf{Temporal Resolution}: Weekly to bi-weekly observations during
  growing season
\item
  \textbf{Spatial Resolution}: County-level aggregated values
\item
  \textbf{Years Covered}: 2018-2021 for model development and testing
  Loading
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{Input Features (X)}\label{input-features-x}

The input data for our models (\texttt{X\_train.npy},
\texttt{X\_test.npy}, \texttt{{[}year{]}\_X.npy}) are time series with a
shape of \texttt{(samples,\ timesteps,\ features)}, where
\texttt{timesteps} represent 6 phenological stages and \texttt{features}
include 14 predictors:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{EVI2 (Enhanced Vegetation Index 2):}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \emph{Description:} A satellite-derived measure of vegetation
    greenness and canopy health.
  \item
    \emph{Significance for Yield:} Higher EVI2 generally indicates a
    healthier, more photosynthetically active crop, which is essential
    for biomass accumulation and ultimately for producing higher yields
    through processes like pod development and seed fill. Stress events
    affecting EVI2 can signal potential yield reductions.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{LST\_Day (Daytime Land Surface Temperature in °C):}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \emph{Description:} The temperature of the ground surface during the
    day.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{LST\_Night (Nighttime Land Surface Temperature in °C):}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \emph{Description:} The temperature of the ground surface during the
    night.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{tmax (Maximum daily air temperature in °C):}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \emph{Description:} Highest air temperature recorded in a day.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{tmin (Minimum daily air temperature in °C):}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \emph{Description:} Lowest air temperature recorded in a day.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{ppt (Precipitation in mm):}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \emph{Description:} Accumulated rainfall.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{vpdmax \& vpdmin (Maximum/Minimum Vapor Pressure Deficit in
  hPa):}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \emph{Description:} Measure of atmospheric dryness (the difference
    between how much moisture the air can hold and how much it actually
    holds).
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Evap\_tavg (Average Evapotranspiration in kg/m²/s or mm/day):}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \emph{Description:} Actual water loss from the soil surface
    (evaporation) and plant tissues (transpiration).
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{PotEvap\_tavg (Average Potential Evapotranspiration in W/m² or
  mm/day):}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \emph{Description:} The amount of evapotranspiration that would
    occur if sufficient water were available.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{SoilMoi0\_10cm (Soil moisture at 0-10 cm depth in kg/m² or
  mm):}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \emph{Description:} Water content in the top soil.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{SoilMoi10\_40cm, SoilMoi40\_100cm, SoilMoi100\_200cm (Soil
  moisture at increasing depths):}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \emph{Description:} Water content in deeper soil layers.
  \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{Target Variable (Y)}\label{target-variable-y}

The target variable for prediction (\texttt{Y\_train.npy},
\texttt{Y\_test.npy}) is: * \textbf{County-Level Soybean Yield:} *
\emph{Unit:} Bushels per acre (bu/ac). * \emph{Significance:} This is
the primary measure of agricultural productivity for soybeans. Accurate
and timely yield prediction is crucial for farmers, policymakers,
insurers, and commodity markets for planning, risk assessment, and
economic forecasting.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# {-}{-}{-} Automatic Data Download and Extraction {-}{-}{-}}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ urllib.request}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ zipfile}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ shutil}

    \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ os.path.exists(file\_path):}
        \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"✓ Found: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\BuiltInTok{file}\SpecialCharTok{\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
    \ControlFlowTok{else}\NormalTok{:}
        \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"✗ Missing: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\BuiltInTok{file}\SpecialCharTok{\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Load preprocessed time series data}

\subsection{Visualizing Input Feature
Dynamics}\label{visualizing-input-feature-dynamics}

To provide a more intuitive understanding of the input data (\texttt{X})
fed into our models, the plots below showcase the time series for three
key predictors---EVI2, Maximum Temperature, and Precipitation---across
the six phenological stages. These visualizations are for three randomly
selected county-year samples from the training dataset and display the
data in its \emph{{[}Specify: `original (pre-normalization)' OR
`normalized'{]}} form.

Observing these plots helps to: * Illustrate the temporal patterns of
different environmental variables through the defined soybean growth
stages. * Appreciate the sample-to-sample variability in these
predictors. * Better understand the nature of the 3D input
\texttt{(samples,\ timesteps,\ features)} that the LSTM and 1D-CNN
models process. Each line in a subplot represents the sequence of values
for one feature across the 6 phenological stages (timesteps) for one
sample.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# === DATA NORMALIZATION FUNCTIONS ===}
\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ normalize\_data(data, mean, std):}
    \CommentTok{"""}
\CommentTok{    Normalize time series data using z{-}score normalization.}

\CommentTok{    This function standardizes each feature across all samples and timesteps}
\CommentTok{    using the training set statistics to prevent data leakage.}

\CommentTok{    Parameters:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    data : numpy.ndarray}
\CommentTok{        Input data of shape (samples, timesteps, features)}
\CommentTok{    mean : numpy.ndarray}
\CommentTok{        Feature{-}wise mean values from training data}
\CommentTok{    std : numpy.ndarray}
\CommentTok{        Feature{-}wise standard deviation from training data}

\CommentTok{    Returns:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    normalized\_data : numpy.ndarray}
\CommentTok{        Z{-}score normalized data}
\CommentTok{    """}
    \CommentTok{\# Prevent division by zero for constant features}
\NormalTok{    std\_safe }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ std.copy()}
\NormalTok{    std\_safe[std\_safe }\OperatorTok{==} \DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{] }\OperatorTok{=} \FloatTok{1e{-}8}

\NormalTok{    normalized\_data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ (data }\OperatorTok{{-}}\NormalTok{ mean) }\OperatorTok{/}\NormalTok{ std\_safe}
    \ControlFlowTok{return}\NormalTok{ normalized\_data}


\CommentTok{\# === COMPUTE NORMALIZATION STATISTICS ===}
\CommentTok{\# Calculate feature{-}wise statistics from training data only}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"}\CharTok{\textbackslash{}n}\StringTok{Calculating normalization statistics from training data..."}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{X\_mean }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.nanmean(X\_train, axis}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{))  }\CommentTok{\# Mean across samples and timesteps}
\NormalTok{X\_std }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.nanstd(X\_train, axis}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{))    }\CommentTok{\# Std across samples and timesteps}

\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Features with zero variance: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{np}\SpecialCharTok{.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(X\_std }\OperatorTok{==} \DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{)}\SpecialCharTok{\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Features with NaN values: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{np}\SpecialCharTok{.}\BuiltInTok{sum}\NormalTok{(np.isnan(X\_mean))}\SpecialCharTok{\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Apply normalization to both training and test sets}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Applying z{-}score normalization..."}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{X\_train\_normalized }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ normalize\_data(X\_train, X\_mean, X\_std)}
\NormalTok{X\_test\_normalized }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ normalize\_data(X\_test, X\_mean, X\_std)}

\CommentTok{\# Update variables for consistency with rest of notebook}
\NormalTok{X\_train }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ X\_train\_normalized}
\NormalTok{X\_test }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ X\_test\_normalized}

\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Data loading and preprocessing complete!"}\NormalTok{)}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Training data statistics: mean=}\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{np}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{nanmean(X\_train)}\SpecialCharTok{:.3f\}}\SpecialStringTok{, std=}\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{np}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{nanstd(X\_train)}\SpecialCharTok{:.3f\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Test data statistics: mean=}\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{np}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{nanmean(X\_test)}\SpecialCharTok{:.3f\}}\SpecialStringTok{, std=}\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{np}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{nanstd(X\_test)}\SpecialCharTok{:.3f\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\section{Why Phenology-Guided Time Series
Modeling?}\label{why-phenology-guided-time-series-modeling}

Crop growth and yield formation are fundamentally governed by
\textbf{phenological development}, not by fixed calendar dates.
Environmental stresses such as heat, water deficit, or excessive
moisture can have vastly different impacts on final yield depending on
\emph{when} they occur during the growing season. For example, stress
during flowering or grain filling often has a disproportionately large
effect compared to similar conditions during early vegetative growth.

Many existing yield prediction approaches rely on calendar-based
temporal aggregation (e.g., weekly or monthly averages). While
convenient, these fixed intervals may mix multiple developmental stages
or split critical growth phases, thereby obscuring biologically
meaningful signals.

In this notebook, we adopt a \textbf{phenology-guided framework}, where
satellite- derived phenological transition dates are used to divide the
growing season into six biologically meaningful stages. Environmental
and vegetation predictors are aggregated within these adaptive stage
boundaries, ensuring that the input time series aligns with actual crop
development rather than arbitrary time windows. This approach improves
both interpretability and the model's ability to learn stage-specific
yield sensitivities.

\section{Why Quantify Prediction
Uncertainty?}\label{why-quantify-prediction-uncertainty}

Crop yield prediction is inherently uncertain due to multiple sources of
variability, including weather fluctuations, observation noise in remote
sensing data, spatial heterogeneity in agricultural systems, and
limitations in model structure. Deterministic point predictions alone do
not convey how reliable a prediction is, which limits their usefulness
for decision-making, risk assessment, and interpretation under atypical
conditions.

To address this limitation, all models implemented in this notebook are
formulated as \textbf{probabilistic models}, producing both a mean yield
estimate and an associated uncertainty. These uncertainty estimates
provide additional context about prediction confidence, highlighting
conditions, regions, or yield ranges where the model is less certain.
This is particularly important for applications such as agricultural
monitoring, insurance, and climate risk assessment, where understanding
prediction reliability is as critical as the prediction itself.

\section{2. Model Development and
Training}\label{model-development-and-training}

This section implements and compares three different approaches for
probabilistic crop yield prediction:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Probabilistic LSTM}: Captures temporal dependencies in crop
  development
\item
  \textbf{Probabilistic 1D-CNN}: Learns local temporal patterns and
  seasonal cycles
\item
  \textbf{Gaussian Process Regression (GPR)}: Provides natural
  uncertainty quantification
\end{enumerate}

All models output both mean predictions and uncertainty estimates,
enabling robust decision-making in agricultural applications.

\subsection{Key Implementation
Features:}\label{key-implementation-features}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Reproducible training}: Fixed random seeds across all models
\item
  \textbf{Early stopping}: Prevents overfitting during neural network
  training
\item
  \textbf{Validation split}: 80/20 train/validation split for
  hyperparameter tuning
\item
  \textbf{Probabilistic outputs}: All models provide prediction
  uncertainty estimates
\end{itemize}

\subsection{2.1 Probabilistic Long Short-Term Memory (LSTM)
Model}\label{probabilistic-long-short-term-memory-lstm-model}

\textbf{Model Rationale:} LSTM networks excel at modeling sequential
data with long-term dependencies, making them ideal for crop yield
prediction where: - Early season conditions influence late season
development - Critical growth stages occur at different times - Weather
patterns show temporal autocorrelation

\textbf{Architecture Details:} - \textbf{Input Layer}: Accepts time
series of shape (timesteps, features) - \textbf{LSTM Layer}: 100 hidden
units with built-in memory mechanisms - \textbf{Dense Layers}: 100-unit
ReLU layer followed by 2-unit output - \textbf{Probabilistic Output}:
Learns both mean (μ) and uncertainty (σ) parameters

\textbf{Training Configuration:} - \textbf{Loss Function}: Negative
Log-Likelihood (NLL) for probabilistic training - \textbf{Optimizer}:
Adam with learning rate 1e-4 - \textbf{Batch Size}: 64 samples -
\textbf{Early Stopping}: Monitors validation loss with patience=10

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# === PROBABILISTIC LSTM MODEL IMPLEMENTATION ===}

\CommentTok{\# Split training data for validation}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Creating train/validation split..."}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{X\_train\_split, X\_val, Y\_train\_split, Y\_val }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ train\_test\_split(}
\NormalTok{    X\_train, Y\_train,}
\NormalTok{    test\_size}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{0.2}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    random\_state}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{42}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{    shuffle}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}
\NormalTok{)}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Train samples: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{X\_train\_split}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{shape[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{]}\SpecialCharTok{\}}\SpecialStringTok{, Validation samples: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{X\_val}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{shape[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{]}\SpecialCharTok{\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# === PROBABILISTIC DISTRIBUTION SETUP ===}

\NormalTok{tfd }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ tfp.distributions}

\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ normal\_sp(params):}
    \CommentTok{"""}
\CommentTok{    Create a Normal distribution from neural network outputs.}

\CommentTok{    This function transforms raw network outputs into a well{-}behaved}
\CommentTok{    probability distribution with learnable mean and variance.}

\CommentTok{    Parameters:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    params : tf.Tensor}
\CommentTok{        Network output tensor with shape (batch\_size, 2)}
\CommentTok{        First column: raw mean values}
\CommentTok{        Second column: raw scale parameters}

\CommentTok{    Returns:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    distribution : tfp.distributions.Normal}
\CommentTok{        Parameterized Normal distribution}
\CommentTok{    """}
    \ControlFlowTok{return}\NormalTok{ tfd.Normal(}
\NormalTok{        loc}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{params[:, }\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{:}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{],  }\CommentTok{\# Mean parameter (no transformation)}
\NormalTok{        scale}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{1e{-}3} \OperatorTok{+}\NormalTok{ tf.math.softplus(}\FloatTok{0.05} \OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ params[:, }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{:}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{])  }\CommentTok{\# Ensure positive scale}
\NormalTok{    )}

\KeywordTok{class}\NormalTok{ ProbabilisticLayer(tf.keras.layers.Layer):}
    \CommentTok{"""}
\CommentTok{    Custom Keras layer that outputs distribution parameters.}

\CommentTok{    This layer takes the raw outputs from the dense layer and}
\CommentTok{    formats them for probabilistic prediction.}
\CommentTok{    """}
    \KeywordTok{def} \FunctionTok{\_\_init\_\_}\NormalTok{(}\VariableTok{self}\NormalTok{, }\OperatorTok{**}\NormalTok{kwargs):}
        \BuiltInTok{super}\NormalTok{().}\FunctionTok{\_\_init\_\_}\NormalTok{(}\OperatorTok{**}\NormalTok{kwargs)}

    \KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ call(}\VariableTok{self}\NormalTok{, inputs):}
        \CommentTok{"""Transform inputs into distribution parameters."""}
\NormalTok{        dist }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ normal\_sp(inputs)}
        \ControlFlowTok{return}\NormalTok{ tf.concat([dist.loc, dist.scale], axis}\OperatorTok{={-}}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{)}

\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ NLL(y\_true, y\_pred):}
    \CommentTok{"""}
\CommentTok{    Negative Log{-}Likelihood loss for probabilistic training.}

\CommentTok{    This loss function encourages the model to:}
\CommentTok{    1. Make accurate mean predictions}
\CommentTok{    2. Provide appropriate uncertainty estimates}
\CommentTok{    3. Avoid overconfident or underconfident predictions}

\CommentTok{    Parameters:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    y\_true : tf.Tensor}
\CommentTok{        True target values}
\CommentTok{    y\_pred : tf.Tensor}
\CommentTok{        Predicted distribution parameters [mean, scale]}

\CommentTok{    Returns:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    nll : tf.Tensor}
\CommentTok{        Negative log{-}likelihood loss value}
\CommentTok{    """}
\NormalTok{    dist }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ tfd.Normal(}
\NormalTok{        loc}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{y\_pred[:, }\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{:}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{],}
\NormalTok{        scale}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{y\_pred[:, }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{:}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{]}
\NormalTok{    )}
    \ControlFlowTok{return} \OperatorTok{{-}}\NormalTok{tf.reduce\_mean(dist.log\_prob(y\_true))}

\CommentTok{\# === REPRODUCIBILITY SETUP ===}

\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ set\_seeds(seed\_value}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{32}\NormalTok{):}
    \CommentTok{"""Set all random seeds for reproducible results."""}
\NormalTok{    os.environ[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}PYTHONHASHSEED\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{] }\OperatorTok{=} \BuiltInTok{str}\NormalTok{(seed\_value)}
\NormalTok{    random.seed(seed\_value)}
\NormalTok{    np.random.seed(seed\_value)}
\NormalTok{    tf.random.set\_seed(seed\_value)}

\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ create\_probabilistic\_lstm(input\_shape, lstm\_units}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{100}\NormalTok{, dense\_units}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{100}\NormalTok{):}
    \CommentTok{"""}
\CommentTok{    Create a probabilistic LSTM model for yield prediction.}

\CommentTok{    Parameters:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    input\_shape : tuple}
\CommentTok{        Shape of input time series (timesteps, features)}
\CommentTok{    lstm\_units : int}
\CommentTok{        Number of LSTM hidden units}
\CommentTok{    dense\_units : int}
\CommentTok{        Number of dense layer units}

\CommentTok{    Returns:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    model : tf.keras.Model}
\CommentTok{        Compiled probabilistic LSTM model}
\CommentTok{    """}
\NormalTok{    model }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Sequential([}
\NormalTok{        Input(shape}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{input\_shape),}
\NormalTok{        LSTM(lstm\_units, name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}lstm\_layer\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{        Dense(dense\_units, activation}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}relu\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}dense\_hidden\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{        Dense(}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{, name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}distribution\_params\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{),  }\CommentTok{\# Output: [mean, scale]}
\NormalTok{        ProbabilisticLayer(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}probabilistic\_output\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    ])}

\NormalTok{    model.}\BuiltInTok{compile}\NormalTok{(}
\NormalTok{        optimizer}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{tf.keras.optimizers.Adam(learning\_rate}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{1e{-}4}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{        loss}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{NLL,}
\NormalTok{        metrics}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}mse\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]  }\CommentTok{\# Additional metric for monitoring}
\NormalTok{    )}

    \ControlFlowTok{return}\NormalTok{ model}

\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ train\_and\_evaluate\_lstm(X\_train\_split, Y\_train\_split, X\_val, Y\_val, X\_test, Y\_test):}
    \CommentTok{"""}
\CommentTok{    Complete training and evaluation pipeline for LSTM model.}

\CommentTok{    Parameters:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    X\_train, Y\_train : numpy.ndarray}
\CommentTok{        Training data and labels}
\CommentTok{    X\_val, Y\_val : numpy.ndarray}
\CommentTok{        Validation data and labels}
\CommentTok{    X\_test, Y\_test : numpy.ndarray}
\CommentTok{        Test data and labels}


\CommentTok{    Returns:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    model : tf.keras.Model}
\CommentTok{        Trained model}
\CommentTok{    mean : numpy.ndarray}
\CommentTok{        Mean predictions for test data}
\CommentTok{    uncertainty : numpy.ndarray}
\CommentTok{        Uncertainty estimates for test data}
\CommentTok{    history : tf.keras.callbacks.History}
\CommentTok{        Training history}
\CommentTok{    """}

    \CommentTok{\# Set seeds for reproducibility}
\NormalTok{    set\_seeds()}

    \CommentTok{\# Create model}
\NormalTok{    model }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ create\_probabilistic\_lstm(input\_shape}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{(X\_train\_split.shape[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{], X\_train\_split.shape[}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{]))}

    \CommentTok{\# Define callbacks}
\NormalTok{    early\_stopping }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ EarlyStopping(}
\NormalTok{        monitor}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}val\_loss\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{        patience}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{        restore\_best\_weights}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{        mode}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}min\textquotesingle{}}
\NormalTok{    )}

    \CommentTok{\# Train the model}
\NormalTok{    history }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ model.fit(}
\NormalTok{        X\_train\_split, Y\_train\_split,}
\NormalTok{        epochs}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{1000}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{        batch\_size}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{64}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{        validation\_data}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{(X\_val, Y\_val),}
\NormalTok{        callbacks}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[early\_stopping],}
\NormalTok{        verbose}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{1}
\NormalTok{    )}

    \CommentTok{\# Get predictions}
\NormalTok{    predictions }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ model.predict(X\_test)}
\NormalTok{    means }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ predictions[:, }\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{]}
\NormalTok{    uncertainties }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ predictions[:, }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{]}

    \CommentTok{\# Calculate metrics}
\NormalTok{    final\_r2 }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ r2\_score(Y\_test, means)}
\NormalTok{    final\_rmse }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.sqrt(mean\_squared\_error(Y\_test, means))}

    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"}\CharTok{\textbackslash{}n}\SpecialStringTok{Final Test Metrics:"}\NormalTok{)}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"R2 Score: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{final\_r2}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"RMSE: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{final\_rmse}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Average Uncertainty: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{np}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{mean(uncertainties)}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}

    \ControlFlowTok{return}\NormalTok{ model, means, uncertainties, history}

\CommentTok{\# Execute LSTM training and evaluation}
\NormalTok{lstm\_model, lstm\_means, lstm\_uncertainties, lstm\_history }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ train\_and\_evaluate\_lstm(}
\NormalTok{    X\_train\_split, Y\_train\_split,}
\NormalTok{    X\_val, Y\_val,}
\NormalTok{    X\_test, Y\_test}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# {-}{-}{-} Plotting Training and Validation Loss (Full and Zoomed Views) {-}{-}{-}}

\CommentTok{\# Ensure \textquotesingle{}history\textquotesingle{} is the Keras History object from model.fit()}

\NormalTok{fig, axes }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ plt.subplots(nrows}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{, ncols}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{, figsize}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{16}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{6}\NormalTok{)) }\CommentTok{\# Adjust figsize as needed}

\NormalTok{history }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ lstm\_history}

\CommentTok{\# Subplot 1: Full Training and Validation Loss Curve}
\NormalTok{axes[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{].plot(history.history[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}loss\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{], label}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Training NLL\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{axes[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{].plot(history.history[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}val\_loss\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{], label}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Validation NLL\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{axes[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{].set\_title(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Full Training \& Validation Loss Curve\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{axes[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{].set\_xlabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Epoch\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{axes[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{].set\_ylabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}NLL (Negative Log{-}Likelihood)\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{axes[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{].legend()}
\NormalTok{axes[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{].grid(}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{, linestyle}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}{-}{-}\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, alpha}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{0.6}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Subplot 2: Zoomed{-}in View of Training and Validation Loss}
\NormalTok{start\_epoch\_for\_zoom }\OperatorTok{=} \DecValTok{200}  \CommentTok{\# Keep this or adjust if another start point is better}
\CommentTok{\# Ensure there are enough epochs to make a zoomed plot meaningful}
\ControlFlowTok{if} \BuiltInTok{len}\NormalTok{(history.history[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}loss\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]) }\OperatorTok{\textgreater{}}\NormalTok{ start\_epoch\_for\_zoom:}
    \CommentTok{\# X{-}axis range for the zoomed plot (actual epoch numbers)}
\NormalTok{    epoch\_range\_zoomed }\OperatorTok{=} \BuiltInTok{range}\NormalTok{(start\_epoch\_for\_zoom, }\BuiltInTok{len}\NormalTok{(history.history[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}loss\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]))}

\NormalTok{    axes[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{].plot(epoch\_range\_zoomed,}
\NormalTok{                 history.history[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}loss\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{][start\_epoch\_for\_zoom:],}
\NormalTok{                 label}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Training NLL (Zoomed)\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    axes[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{].plot(epoch\_range\_zoomed,}
\NormalTok{                 history.history[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}val\_loss\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{][start\_epoch\_for\_zoom:],}
\NormalTok{                 label}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Validation NLL (Zoomed)\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    axes[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{].set\_title(}\SpecialStringTok{f\textquotesingle{}Zoomed Loss (Epochs }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{start\_epoch\_for\_zoom}\SpecialCharTok{\}}\SpecialStringTok{+)\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    axes[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{].set\_xlabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Epoch\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    axes[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{].set\_ylabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}NLL (Negative Log{-}Likelihood)\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    axes[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{].legend()}
\NormalTok{    axes[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{].grid(}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{, linestyle}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}{-}{-}\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, alpha}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{0.6}\NormalTok{)}
\ControlFlowTok{else}\NormalTok{:}
    \CommentTok{\# Fallback if not enough epochs for the defined zoom}
\NormalTok{    axes[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{].text(}\FloatTok{0.5}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{0.5}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Not enough epochs for zoomed view.\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{                 horizontalalignment}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}center\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, verticalalignment}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}center\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{                 transform}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{axes[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{].transAxes)}
\NormalTok{    axes[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{].set\_title(}\SpecialStringTok{f\textquotesingle{}Zoomed View (Epochs }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{start\_epoch\_for\_zoom}\SpecialCharTok{\}}\SpecialStringTok{+)\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    axes[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{].set\_xlabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Epoch\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    axes[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{].set\_ylabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}NLL\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}


\NormalTok{plt.tight\_layout()}
\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\includegraphics{05_Time_Series/01__Soybean_Yield_Prediction/notebooks/Crop_yield_estimationR4_files/figure-pdf/cell-9-output-1.png}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ evaluate\_model(model, X\_test, Y\_test, model\_name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"Model"}\NormalTok{):}
    \CommentTok{"""}
\CommentTok{    Comprehensive evaluation of a probabilistic model.}

\CommentTok{    Parameters:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    model : tf.keras.Model or sklearn model}
\CommentTok{        Trained probabilistic model}
\CommentTok{    X\_test, Y\_test : numpy.ndarray}
\CommentTok{        Test data and labels}
\CommentTok{    model\_name : str}
\CommentTok{        Name of the model for reporting}

\CommentTok{    Returns:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    predictions : numpy.ndarray}
\CommentTok{        Model predictions [mean, uncertainty]}
\CommentTok{    """}
\NormalTok{    predictions }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ model.predict(X\_test)}
\NormalTok{    mean\_pred }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ predictions[:, }\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{]}
\NormalTok{    std\_pred }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ predictions[:, }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{]}

    \CommentTok{\# Calculate metrics}
\NormalTok{    final\_r2 }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ r2\_score(Y\_test, mean\_pred)}
\NormalTok{    final\_rmse }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.sqrt(mean\_squared\_error(Y\_test, mean\_pred))}

    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"}\CharTok{\textbackslash{}n}\SpecialStringTok{Final Test Metrics:"}\NormalTok{)}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"R2 Score: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{final\_r2}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"RMSE: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{final\_rmse}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Mean Prediction Uncertainty: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{np}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{mean(std\_pred)}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Min Uncertainty: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{np}\SpecialCharTok{.}\BuiltInTok{min}\NormalTok{(std\_pred)}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Max Uncertainty: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{np}\SpecialCharTok{.}\BuiltInTok{max}\NormalTok{(std\_pred)}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}

    \CommentTok{\# Calculate prediction interval coverage}
\NormalTok{    within\_interval }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.}\BuiltInTok{abs}\NormalTok{(Y\_test }\OperatorTok{{-}}\NormalTok{ mean\_pred) }\OperatorTok{\textless{}=} \DecValTok{2} \OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ std\_pred}
\NormalTok{    coverage }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.mean(within\_interval) }\OperatorTok{*} \DecValTok{100}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"95\% CI Coverage: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{coverage}\SpecialCharTok{:.2f\}}\SpecialStringTok{\%"}\NormalTok{)}

    \ControlFlowTok{return}\NormalTok{ predictions}

\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ plot\_predictions\_with\_uncertainty(Y\_test, predictions, title}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"Predictions with 95\% Confidence Interval"}\NormalTok{):}
    \CommentTok{"""}
\CommentTok{    Create publication{-}quality prediction vs truth plot with uncertainty visualization.}

\CommentTok{    Parameters:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    Y\_test : numpy.ndarray}
\CommentTok{        True target values}
\CommentTok{    predictions : numpy.ndarray}
\CommentTok{        Model predictions [mean, uncertainty]}
\CommentTok{    """}
\NormalTok{    mean\_pred }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ predictions[:, }\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{]}
\NormalTok{    std\_pred }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ predictions[:, }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{]}

\NormalTok{    plt.figure(figsize}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{8}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{8}\NormalTok{))}

    \CommentTok{\# Calculate overall min and max for consistent axes}
\NormalTok{    all\_values }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.concatenate([Y\_test.flatten(), mean\_pred.flatten()])}
\NormalTok{    min\_val }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ all\_values.}\BuiltInTok{min}\NormalTok{()}
\NormalTok{    max\_val }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ all\_values.}\BuiltInTok{max}\NormalTok{()}

    \CommentTok{\# Add some padding to the limits}
\NormalTok{    padding }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ (max\_val }\OperatorTok{{-}}\NormalTok{ min\_val) }\OperatorTok{*} \FloatTok{0.05}
\NormalTok{    axis\_min }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ min\_val }\OperatorTok{{-}}\NormalTok{ padding}
\NormalTok{    axis\_max }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ max\_val }\OperatorTok{+}\NormalTok{ padding}

    \CommentTok{\# Sort for proper uncertainty band plotting}
\NormalTok{    sort\_idx }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.argsort(Y\_test.flatten())}
\NormalTok{    Y\_test\_sorted }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Y\_test.flatten()[sort\_idx]}
\NormalTok{    mean\_pred\_sorted }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ mean\_pred.flatten()[sort\_idx]}
\NormalTok{    std\_pred\_sorted }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ std\_pred.flatten()[sort\_idx]}

    \CommentTok{\# Plot uncertainty bands}
\NormalTok{    plt.fill\_between(Y\_test\_sorted,}
\NormalTok{                    mean\_pred\_sorted }\OperatorTok{{-}} \DecValTok{2}\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{std\_pred\_sorted,}
\NormalTok{                    mean\_pred\_sorted }\OperatorTok{+} \DecValTok{2}\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{std\_pred\_sorted,}
\NormalTok{                    alpha}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{0.2}\NormalTok{, color}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}coral\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, label}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}95\% CI\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

    \CommentTok{\# Plot predictions}
\NormalTok{    plt.scatter(Y\_test, mean\_pred, alpha}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{0.5}\NormalTok{, color}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}cornflowerblue\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, label}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Predictions\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

    \CommentTok{\# Plot diagonal line}
\NormalTok{    plt.plot([Y\_test.}\BuiltInTok{min}\NormalTok{(), Y\_test.}\BuiltInTok{max}\NormalTok{()],}
\NormalTok{             [Y\_test.}\BuiltInTok{min}\NormalTok{(), Y\_test.}\BuiltInTok{max}\NormalTok{()],}
             \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}r{-}{-}\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, label}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Perfect Prediction\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

    \CommentTok{\# Calculate slope using linear regression}
\NormalTok{    lr }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ LinearRegression()}
\NormalTok{    lr.fit(Y\_test.reshape(}\OperatorTok{{-}}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{), mean\_pred)}
\NormalTok{    slope }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ lr.coef\_[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{]}
\NormalTok{    intercept }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ lr.intercept\_}
\NormalTok{    r2 }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ r2\_score(Y\_test, mean\_pred)}

    \CommentTok{\# Plot fitted regression line}
\NormalTok{    plt.plot([axis\_min, axis\_max],}
\NormalTok{             [slope }\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ axis\_min }\OperatorTok{+}\NormalTok{ intercept, slope }\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ axis\_max }\OperatorTok{+}\NormalTok{ intercept],}
             \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}g{-}\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, alpha}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{0.8}\NormalTok{, linewidth}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{, label}\OperatorTok{=}\SpecialStringTok{f\textquotesingle{}Fitted Line (slope=}\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{slope}\SpecialCharTok{:.2f\}}\SpecialStringTok{)\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

    \CommentTok{\# Set consistent square axes limits}
\NormalTok{    plt.xlim(axis\_min, axis\_max)}
\NormalTok{    plt.ylim(axis\_min, axis\_max)}
\NormalTok{    plt.gca().set\_aspect(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}equal\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, adjustable}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}box\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)  }\CommentTok{\# Make the plot square}

\NormalTok{    plt.xlabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}True Vaules (bu/ac)\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, fontsize}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{18}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    plt.ylabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Predictions (bu/ac)\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, fontsize}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{18}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    plt.xticks(fontsize}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{16}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    plt.yticks(fontsize}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{16}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    plt.title(title, fontsize}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{20}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    plt.legend(fontsize}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{16}\NormalTok{, loc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}upper left\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,frameon}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{False}\NormalTok{)}
    \CommentTok{\# plt.grid(True, alpha=0.3)}
\NormalTok{    plt.tight\_layout()}
\NormalTok{    plt.show()}

\CommentTok{\# Evaluate LSTM model}
\NormalTok{predictions }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ evaluate\_model(lstm\_model, X\_test, Y\_test, model\_name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"LSTM"}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Visualize LSTM results}
\NormalTok{plot\_predictions\_with\_uncertainty(Y\_test, predictions)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsection{2.2 Probabilistic 1D Convolutional Neural Network (CNN)
Model}\label{probabilistic-1d-convolutional-neural-network-cnn-model}

\textbf{Model Rationale:} 1D CNNs are particularly effective for time
series analysis because they: - Detect local temporal patterns and
seasonal cycles - Require fewer parameters than LSTM networks - Process
data more efficiently for shorter sequences - Capture
translation-invariant patterns across the growing season

\textbf{Architecture Design:} - \textbf{Multi-scale Feature Extraction}:
Three convolutional blocks with different receptive fields -
\textbf{Hierarchical Learning}: Filters progress from 32→32→16 to learn
features at multiple scales - \textbf{Pooling Strategy}: MaxPooling
reduces temporal dimension while preserving important features -
\textbf{Probabilistic Head}: Same as LSTM - outputs mean and uncertainty
estimates

\textbf{Key Differences from LSTM:} - \textbf{Computational Efficiency}:
Faster training and inference - \textbf{Local Pattern Focus}: Better at
detecting short-term temporal signatures - \textbf{Parameter
Efficiency}: Fewer trainable parameters than equivalent LSTM -
\textbf{Parallel Processing}: Convolutions can be parallelized more
effectively

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]

\CommentTok{\# === PROBABILISTIC 1D{-}CNN MODEL IMPLEMENTATION ===}

\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ create\_probabilistic\_cnn(input\_shape, filters}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\DecValTok{32}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{32}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{16}\NormalTok{], kernel\_size}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{3}\NormalTok{, dense\_units}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{100}\NormalTok{):}
    \CommentTok{"""}
\CommentTok{    Create a probabilistic 1D{-}CNN model for yield prediction.}

\CommentTok{    Parameters:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    input\_shape : tuple}
\CommentTok{        Shape of input time series (timesteps, features)}
\CommentTok{    filters : list}
\CommentTok{        Number of filters for each convolutional layer}
\CommentTok{    kernel\_size : int}
\CommentTok{        Size of convolutional kernels}
\CommentTok{    dense\_units : int}
\CommentTok{        Number of dense layer units}

\CommentTok{    Returns:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    model : tf.keras.Model}
\CommentTok{        Compiled probabilistic CNN model}
\CommentTok{    """}
\NormalTok{    model }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Sequential([}
\NormalTok{        Input(shape}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{input\_shape),}

        \CommentTok{\# First convolutional block {-} captures fine{-}grained patterns}
\NormalTok{        Conv1D(filters}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{filters[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{], kernel\_size}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{kernel\_size,}
\NormalTok{               activation}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}relu\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, padding}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}same\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}conv1d\_1\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{        MaxPooling1D(pool\_size}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{, name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}maxpool\_1\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{),}

        \CommentTok{\# Second convolutional block {-} learns mid{-}level features}
\NormalTok{        Conv1D(filters}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{filters[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{], kernel\_size}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{kernel\_size,}
\NormalTok{               activation}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}relu\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, padding}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}same\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}conv1d\_2\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{        MaxPooling1D(pool\_size}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{, name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}maxpool\_2\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{),}

        \CommentTok{\# Third convolutional block {-} high{-}level temporal abstractions}
\NormalTok{        Conv1D(filters}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{filters[}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{], kernel\_size}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{kernel\_size,}
\NormalTok{               activation}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}relu\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, padding}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}same\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}conv1d\_3\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{),}

        \CommentTok{\# Flatten and dense layers}
\NormalTok{        Flatten(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}flatten\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{        Dense(dense\_units, activation}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}relu\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}dense\_hidden\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{        Dense(}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{, name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}distribution\_params\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{        ProbabilisticLayer(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}probabilistic\_output\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    ])}

\NormalTok{    model.}\BuiltInTok{compile}\NormalTok{(}
\NormalTok{        optimizer}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{tf.keras.optimizers.Adam(learning\_rate}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{1e{-}4}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{        loss}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{NLL,}
\NormalTok{        metrics}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}mse\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}
\NormalTok{    )}

    \ControlFlowTok{return}\NormalTok{ model}

\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ train\_and\_evaluate\_cnn(X\_train, Y\_train, X\_val, Y\_val, X\_test, Y\_test):}
    \CommentTok{"""}
\CommentTok{    Complete training and evaluation pipeline for CNN model.}
\CommentTok{    """}
\NormalTok{    set\_seeds(}\DecValTok{132}\NormalTok{)}

    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Creating 1D{-}CNN model architecture..."}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    model }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ create\_probabilistic\_cnn(}
\NormalTok{        input\_shape}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{(X\_train.shape[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{], X\_train.shape[}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{])}
\NormalTok{    )}
\NormalTok{    model.summary()}

    \CommentTok{\# Define callbacks}
\NormalTok{    early\_stopping }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ EarlyStopping(}
\NormalTok{        monitor}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}val\_loss\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{        patience}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{        restore\_best\_weights}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{        mode}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}min\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{        verbose}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{1}
\NormalTok{    )}

    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"}\CharTok{\textbackslash{}n}\StringTok{Starting CNN training..."}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    history }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ model.fit(}
\NormalTok{        X\_train, Y\_train,}
\NormalTok{        epochs}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{1000}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{        batch\_size}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{64}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{        validation\_data}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{(X\_val, Y\_val),}
\NormalTok{        callbacks}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[early\_stopping],}
\NormalTok{        verbose}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{1}
\NormalTok{    )}

    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"}\CharTok{\textbackslash{}n}\StringTok{Evaluating CNN on test set..."}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    predictions }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ model.predict(X\_test, verbose}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    mean\_pred }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ predictions[:, }\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{]}
\NormalTok{    std\_pred }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ predictions[:, }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{]}

    \CommentTok{\# Calculate performance metrics}
\NormalTok{    r2 }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ r2\_score(Y\_test, mean\_pred)}
\NormalTok{    rmse }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.sqrt(mean\_squared\_error(Y\_test, mean\_pred))}
\NormalTok{    mae }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.mean(np.}\BuiltInTok{abs}\NormalTok{(Y\_test.flatten() }\OperatorTok{{-}}\NormalTok{ mean\_pred))}

    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"}\CharTok{\textbackslash{}n}\SpecialStringTok{=== CNN MODEL PERFORMANCE ==="}\NormalTok{)}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"R² Score: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{r2}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"RMSE: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{rmse}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{ bu/acre"}\NormalTok{)}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"MAE: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{mae}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{ bu/acre"}\NormalTok{)}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Average Uncertainty: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{np}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{mean(std\_pred)}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{ bu/acre"}\NormalTok{)}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Training completed in }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\BuiltInTok{len}\NormalTok{(history.history[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}loss\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{])}\SpecialCharTok{\}}\SpecialStringTok{ epochs"}\NormalTok{)}

    \ControlFlowTok{return}\NormalTok{ model, predictions, history}

\CommentTok{\# Execute CNN training and evaluation}
\NormalTok{cnn\_model, cnn\_predictions, cnn\_history }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ train\_and\_evaluate\_cnn(}
\NormalTok{    X\_train\_split, Y\_train\_split,}
\NormalTok{    X\_val, Y\_val,}
\NormalTok{    X\_test, Y\_test}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}

\end{verbatim}

\begin{verbatim}

\end{verbatim}

\subsection{2.3 Gaussian Process Regression (GPR)
Model}\label{gaussian-process-regression-gpr-model}

\textbf{Model Rationale:} Gaussian Processes provide a Bayesian approach
to regression that: - Naturally quantifies uncertainty without
architectural modifications - Works well with limited training data -
Provides theoretical guarantees about uncertainty calibration - Serves
as a strong baseline for comparison with neural networks

\textbf{Key Advantages:} - \textbf{Natural Uncertainty}: Uncertainty
estimates are theoretically grounded - \textbf{Non-parametric}: Flexible
model that adapts to data complexity - \textbf{Interpretable}: Kernel
functions have clear mathematical meaning - \textbf{Calibrated}:
Uncertainty estimates are typically well-calibrated

\textbf{Implementation Notes:} - \textbf{Computational Complexity}:
O(n³) scaling requires subsampling for large datasets - \textbf{Kernel
Choice}: RBF + White noise kernel for smooth trends with observation
noise - \textbf{Hyperparameter Optimization}: Automatic optimization of
kernel parameters - \textbf{Data Preprocessing}: Requires flattening of
time series for traditional ML interface

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#\#\# Gaussian Process Regression (GPR)}
\CommentTok{\# Set random seed for reproducibility}
\NormalTok{seed\_value}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{11}
\NormalTok{np.random.seed(seed\_value)}
\NormalTok{random.seed(seed\_value)}

\CommentTok{\# Flatten the time series data for GPR}
\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ flatten\_time\_series\_data(X):}
    \CommentTok{"""Flatten time series data for traditional ML models"""}
\NormalTok{    n\_samples, n\_timesteps, n\_features }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ X.shape}
    \ControlFlowTok{return}\NormalTok{ X.reshape(n\_samples, n\_timesteps }\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ n\_features)}

\CommentTok{\# Flatten training and test data}
\NormalTok{X\_train\_flat }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ flatten\_time\_series\_data(X\_train\_split)}
\NormalTok{X\_val\_flat }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ flatten\_time\_series\_data(X\_val)}
\NormalTok{X\_test\_flat }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ flatten\_time\_series\_data(X\_test)}

\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Original shape: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{X\_train\_split}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{shape}\SpecialCharTok{\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Flattened shape: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{X\_train\_flat}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{shape}\SpecialCharTok{\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Due to computational constraints, we\textquotesingle{}ll use a subset for GPR training}
\CommentTok{\# GPR scales as O(n³) so we need to limit the training size}
\NormalTok{max\_samples }\OperatorTok{=} \DecValTok{2000}  \CommentTok{\# Adjust based on your computational resources}
\ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ X\_train\_flat.shape[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{] }\OperatorTok{\textgreater{}}\NormalTok{ max\_samples:}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Using subset of }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{max\_samples}\SpecialCharTok{\}}\SpecialStringTok{ samples for GPR training"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    indices }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.random.choice(X\_train\_flat.shape[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{], max\_samples, replace}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{False}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    X\_train\_gpr }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ X\_train\_flat[indices]}
\NormalTok{    Y\_train\_gpr }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Y\_train\_split[indices].ravel()}
\ControlFlowTok{else}\NormalTok{:}
\NormalTok{    X\_train\_gpr }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ X\_train\_flat}
\NormalTok{    Y\_train\_gpr }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Y\_train\_split.ravel()}

\CommentTok{\# Define the kernel}
\CommentTok{\# We use a combination of RBF (for smooth variations) and WhiteKernel (for noise)}
\NormalTok{kernel }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ C(}\FloatTok{1.0}\NormalTok{, (}\FloatTok{1e{-}3}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{1e3}\NormalTok{)) }\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ RBF(length\_scale}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{1.0}\NormalTok{, length\_scale\_bounds}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{(}\FloatTok{1e{-}2}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{1e2}\NormalTok{)) }\OperatorTok{+}\NormalTok{ WhiteKernel(noise\_level}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{1.0}\NormalTok{, noise\_level\_bounds}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{(}\FloatTok{1e{-}10}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{1e+1}\NormalTok{))}

\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Creating Gaussian Process Regressor..."}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{gpr\_model }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ GaussianProcessRegressor(}
\NormalTok{    kernel}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{kernel,}
\NormalTok{    alpha}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{1e{-}6}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# Small regularization parameter}
\NormalTok{    normalize\_y}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# Normalize target values}
\NormalTok{    n\_restarts\_optimizer}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{5}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# Number of restarts for optimization}
\NormalTok{    random\_state}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{seed\_value,  }\CommentTok{\# Set random seed for reproducibility}
    \CommentTok{\# verbose=1  \# Verbosity level}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Train the GPR model}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Training Gaussian Process Regressor..."}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{start\_time }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ time.time()}
\NormalTok{gpr\_model.fit(X\_train\_gpr, Y\_train\_gpr)}
\NormalTok{training\_time }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ time.time() }\OperatorTok{{-}}\NormalTok{ start\_time}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Training completed in }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{training\_time}\SpecialCharTok{:.2f\}}\SpecialStringTok{ seconds"}\NormalTok{)}

\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Optimized kernel: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{gpr\_model}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{kernel\_}\SpecialCharTok{\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Log{-}marginal{-}likelihood: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{gpr\_model}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{log\_marginal\_likelihood\_value\_}\SpecialCharTok{:.3f\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
Original shape: (2195, 6, 14)
Flattened shape: (2195, 84)
Using subset of 2000 samples for GPR training
Creating Gaussian Process Regressor...
Training Gaussian Process Regressor...
Training completed in 235.27 seconds
Optimized kernel: 1.75**2 * RBF(length_scale=7.02) + WhiteKernel(noise_level=0.0848)
Log-marginal-likelihood: -1077.263
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Make predictions with uncertainty}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Making predictions..."}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Predictions on training set (subset)}
\NormalTok{gpr\_pred\_train, gpr\_std\_train }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ gpr\_model.predict(X\_train\_gpr, return\_std}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Predictions on validation set}
\NormalTok{gpr\_pred\_val, gpr\_std\_val }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ gpr\_model.predict(X\_val\_flat, return\_std}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Predictions on test set}
\NormalTok{gpr\_pred\_test, gpr\_std\_test }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ gpr\_model.predict(X\_test\_flat, return\_std}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Calculate metrics}
\NormalTok{train\_r2 }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ r2\_score(Y\_train\_gpr, gpr\_pred\_train)}
\NormalTok{train\_rmse }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.sqrt(mean\_squared\_error(Y\_train\_gpr, gpr\_pred\_train))}

\NormalTok{val\_r2 }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ r2\_score(Y\_val, gpr\_pred\_val)}
\NormalTok{val\_rmse }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.sqrt(mean\_squared\_error(Y\_val, gpr\_pred\_val))}

\NormalTok{test\_r2 }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ r2\_score(Y\_test, gpr\_pred\_test)}
\NormalTok{test\_rmse }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.sqrt(mean\_squared\_error(Y\_test, gpr\_pred\_test))}

\CommentTok{\# Print results}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"}\CharTok{\textbackslash{}n}\SpecialStringTok{Gaussian Process Regression Model Performance:"}\NormalTok{)}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Test {-} R²: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{test\_r2}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{, RMSE: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{test\_rmse}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"Average Test Uncertainty: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{np}\SpecialCharTok{.}\NormalTok{mean(gpr\_std\_test)}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Calculate prediction interval coverage}
\NormalTok{within\_interval }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.}\BuiltInTok{abs}\NormalTok{(Y\_test.flatten() }\OperatorTok{{-}}\NormalTok{ gpr\_pred\_test) }\OperatorTok{\textless{}=} \DecValTok{2} \OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ gpr\_std\_test}
\NormalTok{coverage }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.mean(within\_interval) }\OperatorTok{*} \DecValTok{100}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"95\% CI Coverage: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{coverage}\SpecialCharTok{:.2f\}}\SpecialStringTok{\%"}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# \# Create scatter plot for GPR predictions}
\NormalTok{plot\_predictions\_with\_uncertainty(Y\_test, np.array([gpr\_pred\_test, gpr\_std\_test]).T)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
Making predictions...

Gaussian Process Regression Model Performance:
Test - R²: 0.4373, RMSE: 3.7534
Average Test Uncertainty: 2.9635
95% CI Coverage: 85.43%
\end{verbatim}

\section{3. Advanced Analysis and
Interpretation}\label{advanced-analysis-and-interpretation}

This section provides deeper insights into model behavior and practical
applications:

\subsection{3.1 Multi-Year Performance
Analysis}\label{multi-year-performance-analysis}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Temporal Generalization}: How well models perform across
  different years
\item
  \textbf{Scatter Plot Analysis}: Visual assessment of prediction
  quality by year
\item
  \textbf{Annual Yield Trends}: Comparison of predicted vs actual yield
  patterns
\end{itemize}

\subsection{3.2 Feature and Temporal
Importance}\label{feature-and-temporal-importance}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Permutation Importance}: Identifies most influential
  environmental variables
\item
  \textbf{Phenological Analysis}: Determines critical growth stages for
  yield prediction
\item
  \textbf{Agricultural Insights}: Translates model behavior into
  agronomic understanding
\end{itemize}

\subsection{3.3 Spatial-Temporal
Visualization}\label{spatial-temporal-visualization}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Geographic Mapping}: County-level prediction and uncertainty
  visualization
\item
  \textbf{Uncertainty Patterns}: Spatial distribution of model
  confidence
\item
  \textbf{Temporal Consistency}: Year-to-year prediction stability
\end{itemize}

\subsection{3.1 Multi-Year Model Performance
Analysis}\label{multi-year-model-performance-analysis}

This section evaluates how well our trained models generalize across
different growing seasons and environmental conditions. By testing on
individual years (2018-2021), we can:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Assess Temporal Robustness}: How consistent are predictions
  across different weather years?
\item
  \textbf{Identify Model Weaknesses}: Which years or conditions
  challenge each model most?
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Key Evaluation Aspects:} - \textbf{Year-by-Year Performance}: R²
and RMSE metrics for each test year - \textbf{Visual Pattern Analysis}:
Scatter plots reveal model behavior and outliers

\subsection{3.2 Feature Importance
Analysis}\label{feature-importance-analysis}

Understanding which environmental variables most strongly influence crop
yield predictions is crucial for:

\textbf{Model Interpretation:} - \textbf{Validate Agricultural
Knowledge}: Confirm model learns biologically meaningful patterns -
\textbf{Identify Model Biases}: Detect if model relies on spurious
correlations - \textbf{Guide Feature Engineering}: Inform future data
collection and preprocessing strategies

\textbf{Scientific Understanding:} - \textbf{Quantify Variable
Importance}: Rank environmental factors by prediction contribution -
\textbf{Regional Adaptation}: Understand which factors matter most in
specific growing regions - \textbf{Climate Change Impacts}: Assess
sensitivity to variables likely to change

\textbf{Methodology:}

We use \textbf{permutation importance} which measures how much model
performance degrades when each feature is randomly shuffled, breaking
its relationship with the target while preserving its distribution.

\textbf{How the \texttt{permutation\_importance} function works:}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Establish Baseline Performance:}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    First, the function calculates a \texttt{baseline\_score} using a
    chosen evaluation \texttt{metric} (e.g., R² score) on the original,
    unaltered test dataset (\texttt{X}, \texttt{y}). This score
    represents the model's performance when all features have their true
    values.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Iterate Through Features:}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    The function then iterates through each input feature one by one
    (e.g., EVI2, LST\_Day, specific soil moisture layers, etc.).
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Permute Feature Values:}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    For the current feature being evaluated, its values are randomly
    shuffled across \emph{all samples and all timesteps} in a
    \emph{copy} of the test dataset (\texttt{X\_permuted}). This
    shuffling breaks the relationship between that feature and the
    target variable (\texttt{y}), effectively making the feature noisy
    or uninformative while keeping other features intact.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Evaluate Performance with Permuted Feature:}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    The model then makes predictions using this \texttt{X\_permuted}
    dataset (where one feature is shuffled).
  \item
    A new performance score (\texttt{permuted\_score}) is calculated
    using the same metric.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Calculate Importance Score:}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    The importance of the feature for that single permutation run is the
    difference between the \texttt{baseline\_score} and the
    \texttt{permuted\_score} (i.e.,
    \texttt{baseline\_score\ -\ permuted\_score}).
  \item
    A significant drop in performance (a high positive importance score)
    after permuting a feature suggests that the model relied heavily on
    that feature for making accurate predictions. If the score does not
    change much, the feature is considered less important.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Repeat for Robustness:}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Steps 3-5 are repeated \texttt{n\_repeats} times (e.g., 10 times by
    default) for each feature, with a new random permutation each time.
  \item
    The average of these repeated importance scores is then taken as the
    final importance score for that feature. This averaging helps to
    provide a more stable and reliable estimate of feature importance.
  \end{itemize}
\end{enumerate}

The output is a list of importance scores, corresponding to each
feature, indicating their relative contributions to the model's
predictive power on the given dataset and metric.

    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}font.size\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: }\DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{,}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}axes.labelsize\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: }\DecValTok{11}\NormalTok{,}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}axes.titlesize\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: }\DecValTok{12}\NormalTok{,}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}xtick.labelsize\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: }\DecValTok{9}\NormalTok{,}

    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}savefig.dpi\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: }\DecValTok{300}\NormalTok{,}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}savefig.bbox\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}tight\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}savefig.pad\_inches\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: }\FloatTok{0.1}
\NormalTok{\})}

\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ permutation\_importance(model, X, y, metric, feature\_names, n\_repeats}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{):}
    \CommentTok{"""}
\CommentTok{    Computes feature importance and its stability (standard deviation)}
\CommentTok{    using the permutation importance method for time{-}series data.}

\CommentTok{    The importance of a feature is determined by measuring the decrease in a model\textquotesingle{}s}
\CommentTok{    performance score when that feature\textquotesingle{}s values are randomly shuffled. A larger drop}
\CommentTok{    in score indicates higher importance. This process is repeated multiple times}
\CommentTok{    (n\_repeats) for each feature to get a mean importance and its standard deviation.}

\CommentTok{    Parameters:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    model : keras.Model}
\CommentTok{        The trained Keras model. Assumes model.predict(X)[:, 0] gives mean predictions.}
\CommentTok{    X : numpy.ndarray}
\CommentTok{        Input data (samples, timesteps, features).}
\CommentTok{    y : numpy.ndarray}
\CommentTok{        True target values.}
\CommentTok{    metric : function}
\CommentTok{        Performance metric function (e.g., r2\_score).}
\CommentTok{    feature\_names : list of str}
\CommentTok{        Names of the features.}
\CommentTok{    n\_repeats : int, optional}
\CommentTok{        Number of times to repeat permutation for each feature. Default is 10.}

\CommentTok{    Returns:}
\CommentTok{    {-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}}
\CommentTok{    feature\_names : list of str}
\CommentTok{        The original list of feature names.}
\CommentTok{    mean\_importances : list of float}
\CommentTok{        Mean importance score for each feature.}
\CommentTok{    std\_importances : list of float}
\CommentTok{        Standard deviation of importance scores for each feature across repeats.}
\CommentTok{    """}
    \CommentTok{\# 1. Calculate the baseline performance score}
\NormalTok{    baseline\_score }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ metric(y, model.predict(X)[:, }\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{])}

\NormalTok{    mean\_importances }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [] }\CommentTok{\# To store mean importance score for each feature}
\NormalTok{    std\_importances }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ []  }\CommentTok{\# To store std dev of importance scores for each feature}

    \CommentTok{\# 2. Iterate over each feature}
    \ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ feature\_idx }\KeywordTok{in} \BuiltInTok{range}\NormalTok{(X.shape[}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{]):}
\NormalTok{        scores\_for\_current\_feature }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [] }\CommentTok{\# Scores from multiple permutations for this feature}

        \CommentTok{\# 3. Repeat permutation n\_repeats times for the current feature}
        \ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ \_ }\KeywordTok{in} \BuiltInTok{range}\NormalTok{(n\_repeats):}
\NormalTok{            X\_permuted }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ X.copy()}

            \CommentTok{\# 4. Permute the current feature across all samples and timesteps}
\NormalTok{            permuted\_values }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.random.permutation(X\_permuted[:, :, feature\_idx].flatten())}

            \CommentTok{\# 5. Reshape and assign permuted values}
\NormalTok{            X\_permuted[:, :, feature\_idx] }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ permuted\_values.reshape(X.shape[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{], X.shape[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{])}

            \CommentTok{\# 6. Calculate score with permuted feature}
\NormalTok{            permuted\_score }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ metric(y, model.predict(X\_permuted)[:, }\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{])}

            \CommentTok{\# 7. Importance is the drop in score}
\NormalTok{            scores\_for\_current\_feature.append(baseline\_score }\OperatorTok{{-}}\NormalTok{ permuted\_score)}

        \CommentTok{\# 8. Calculate mean and std dev of importances from n\_repeats}
\NormalTok{        mean\_importances.append(np.mean(scores\_for\_current\_feature))}
\NormalTok{        std\_importances.append(np.std(scores\_for\_current\_feature))}

    \ControlFlowTok{return}\NormalTok{ feature\_names, mean\_importances, std\_importances}

\CommentTok{\# Define feature names (as in your provided code)}
\CommentTok{\# Ensure this list matches the order and number of features in X\_test correctly}
\NormalTok{non\_soil\_vars }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}EVI2\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}LST\_Day\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}LST\_Night\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}tmax\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}
                 \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}tmin\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}ppt\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}vpdmax\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}vpdmin\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Evap\_tavg\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}
                 \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}PotEvap\_tavg\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}SoilMoi0\_10cm\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}SoilMoi10\_40cm\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}
                 \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}SoilMoi40\_100cm\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}SoilMoi100\_200cm\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}

\CommentTok{\# Calculate importance scores and standard deviations}
\CommentTok{\# Assuming \textquotesingle{}model\textquotesingle{}, \textquotesingle{}X\_test\textquotesingle{}, \textquotesingle{}Y\_test\textquotesingle{}, \textquotesingle{}r2\_score\textquotesingle{} are defined}
\CommentTok{\# This function now returns feature\_names as the first element}
\CommentTok{\# to maintain correspondence if you pass them in.}
\NormalTok{ordered\_feature\_names, mean\_importance\_scores, std\_importance\_scores }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ permutation\_importance(}
\NormalTok{    model, X\_test, Y\_test, r2\_score, non\_soil\_vars, n\_repeats}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{10}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Combine for sorting based on mean importance scores}
\NormalTok{results\_with\_std }\OperatorTok{=} \BuiltInTok{list}\NormalTok{(}\BuiltInTok{zip}\NormalTok{(ordered\_feature\_names, mean\_importance\_scores, std\_importance\_scores))}
\CommentTok{\# Sort by mean importance score in descending order}
\NormalTok{results\_with\_std.sort(key}\OperatorTok{=}\KeywordTok{lambda}\NormalTok{ x: x[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{], reverse}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{)}

\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"}\CharTok{\textbackslash{}n}\StringTok{Feature Importance Rankings (Mean +/{-} Std Dev):"}\NormalTok{)}
\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ feature, score, std\_dev }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ results\_with\_std:}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\SpecialStringTok{f"}\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{feature}\SpecialCharTok{:\textless{}30\}}\SpecialStringTok{ importance: }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{score}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{ +/{-} }\SpecialCharTok{\{}\NormalTok{std\_dev}\SpecialCharTok{:.4f\}}\SpecialStringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Unzip for plotting (features will be in sorted order)}
\NormalTok{sorted\_features, sorted\_scores, sorted\_stds }\OperatorTok{=} \BuiltInTok{zip}\NormalTok{(}\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{results\_with\_std)}

\CommentTok{\# Create a bar plot with error bars}
\NormalTok{plt.figure(figsize}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{14}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{7}\NormalTok{)) }\CommentTok{\# Adjusted figsize for better readability with error bars}
\NormalTok{bars }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ plt.bar(sorted\_features, sorted\_scores, yerr}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{sorted\_stds,}
\NormalTok{               capsize}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{4}\NormalTok{, alpha}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{0.8}\NormalTok{, color}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}cornflowerblue\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, ecolor}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}black\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{) }\CommentTok{\# Added yerr and capsize}

\NormalTok{plt.xticks(rotation}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{45}\NormalTok{, ha}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}right\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, fontsize}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{14}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.yticks(fontsize}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{14}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.xlabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Features\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, fontsize}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{16}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.ylabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Importance Score (Decrease in R²)\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, fontsize}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{16}\NormalTok{) }\CommentTok{\# Clarified y{-}axis}
\NormalTok{plt.title(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Feature Importance Based on Permutation Test (with Stability)\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, fontsize}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{18}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.grid(}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{, axis}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}y\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, linestyle}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}{-}{-}\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, alpha}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{0.7}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.tight\_layout()}
\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}
